중앙은행 지산 매입 171

들리는 바에 따르면 중앙은행은 영업 발전에 따라 확충해야 하므로 현재 은 75만 6천 냥으로 盛氏 愚斋 义庄 자선 기금회 소유 黄浦滩 6호 大英银行 원래 부지를 매입했는데, 면적이 약 2무 5푼 여이고, 그 가치는 中国营业公司에서 평가했다. 이미 어제 거래가 성사되었다.

오늘 은행 결산 휴가 172

오늘 (7월 1일)부터 3일까지 중외 각 은행은 반년 말 결산 기간이므로 예년의 사례에 따라 2일간 휴업한다. 3일은 마침 일요일이므로 올해 봉관은 총 3일이다. 4일부터 정상 영업을 개시한다. 단 화상 은행 중 예전부터 일요일 휴가가 없었던 곳은 반년 결산을 원용하지 않고, 전장 업무와 유사한 곳은 모두 휴업하지 않는다.

감면 임대료 운위원회 시 정부에 방법 공포 요청 173

어제 청원 陈克成 대리 면회

대표는 만족하지 못하여 다시 吴에게 알현할 예정

상해시 감면 임대료 운동위원회는 제3차 대표 대회에서 다음과 같이 결의했다. (1) 시 정부는 본월 말까지 구역별 감면 임대료 방법에 따라 명을 내려 공포할 것. (2) 시 정부는 법원에 감면 방법에 대한 자문 없이 임대료 분쟁에 대해 원정을 집행하도록 요청하고 张一尘, 余华龙, 曹志功, 李永祥, 刘仲英, 陈培德 등을 청원 대표로 추대했다. 이 대표들은 어제 오전 10시에 방문했으나 시 정부에 도착한 후 吴 시장에게 면회를 요청했으나 吴 시장은 시정 회의에 참석하여 면회할 시간이 없어 선전과 주임 陈克成을 접견실에서 연회하고 진술을 받아들였다. 진술한 각 점에 대해 吴 시장에게 속히 실시하도록 전달하겠다고 약속했다. 대표들은 곧 퇴장했으나 吴 씨를 만나지 못해 만족하지 못하여 다시 청원하여 반드시 확실한 답변을 요구할 예정이다.

Dr. Roger's Speech on Chinese Education Problems 174

Dr. Roger, professor at Columbia University in the United States and a renowned new educationist, came to China in March to investigate education in various regions. His footprints spanned the north and south of China. He is now in Shanghai for a short stay before departing for Europe to attend the International New Education Conference. Mr. Li Shizeng and others from the World Society, recognizing that Dr. Roger's investigation of Chinese education would yield many insights and that he would undoubtedly have good suggestions for improvement, specially invited him to deliver a speech on "Chinese Education Problems" at the World College at 393 Fucaixin Road in the French Concession of this city at 11:00 AM on the 26th of last month. Over 400 people attended, including Cai Yuanpei and his wife, Li Shizeng, Gao Lu, Wang Jingqi, Yang Zhaoyun, Qi Zhi, Zhang Zhongdao, Zhang Junqi, Zhang Shijie, Wu Yunzhai, etc. They were first entertained with Chinese tea and snacks in a separate room. The meeting began at 11:00 AM, with an introductory speech by Mr. Li Shizeng, followed by Dr. Roger's speech, which is as follows: "I am extremely honored to meet with all of you today. The greatest problem in the world today is the pursuit of mutual understanding between nations. Without this, the world will inevitably experience great chaos and suffering. Consider that more than a decade has passed since the end of the European War, yet international chaos and suffering persist. This demonstrates that mutual understanding between nations is indeed a serious problem. We must recognize that international understanding and the construction of social education are of equal importance. During the European War, some people said that after this war, we would never see armed conflict again. However, the state of unrest in the world after the war is even worse than before the war. This was something that was not anticipated during the European War. Looking at the economies of the United States, Britain, Germany, France, and Italy, although they have fully developed, the number of unemployed people in America, according to recent statistics, has reached over ten million. The number of unemployed people in Europe is similar. The highest economic development has led to this result, which is largely due to international confrontation. Therefore, we must acknowledge that international understanding is now the most serious issue. To seek international understanding, we must first transform society. If we want to solve the transformation of society, we must first discuss the problem of education. My wife and I came to China for four months and visited various parts of the country. I feel that China needs to apply new education. Although I do not fully understand this problem, I believe that the education in Chinese schools is not suitable for the needs of society. This phenomenon is not unique to China; it is also the case in European and American countries. We should urgently think of ways to improve it. The upcoming International New Education Conference will be held in Europe, and we will try to solve this problem. I believe that the development of Chinese education is unreasonable because Chinese schools focus too much on academics, just like in Europe and America, and they also fail to meet the needs of local culture. There will be 2,000 people attending this New Education Conference, representing 50 countries. They are mostly entrusted by their own organizations to discuss the key points of new education policies. I believe that education must be adapted to the needs of the social environment and should be tailored to local conditions. Each place has its own special circumstances and cannot be generalized. I believe that there are several areas where Chinese education should be improved: (1) Urban education should be changed to rural education because the majority of Chinese people live in rural areas, while only a few live in cities. To ensure the rational development of Chinese education, we must pay attention to rural education. (2) Chinese education should pay attention to limiting population growth because China's population is excessive, and the supply of materials nationwide cannot satisfy everyone. If Chinese hygiene and medicine continue to improve, China's population will not only be 400 million but will increase to 600 million, 800 million, or even 1 billion. At that time, it will inevitably become an obstacle to construction and progress. Therefore, we should pay attention to limiting China's population. (3) Chinese education must promote the development of transportation. Although China has 400 million people, they are unfortunately fragmented and unable to unite, as if they are living in millions of villages without interacting with each other. In fact, due to inconvenient transportation, there is no connection in everything, and education is also fragmented. Therefore, we should first develop transportation and increase the public's opportunity to receive education. (4) The aim of Chinese education policy should not be to cultivate a small number of outstanding individuals but to raise the knowledge of the general public to the same level, both in rural and urban areas. At the same time, promote the education of industrialization and agriculture to support the development of the entire education. (5) Attention should be paid to health education. In implementing education in rural areas, we should make the general public pay attention to health, so that they can receive simple health education and apply it practically to help their health. The above are all the needs偏於 on material aspects. As for intellectual education, it is also important. The so-called need for knowledge is what method should be used to enable the general illiterate population to be literate and the general public to have basic common sense so that they can express their individual will. This is the success of education. We feel that the use of education must be in line with social conditions and put into practice. For example, in Ding County, Hebei, there are 118 university graduates who have nothing to do, forming a high-level parasitic figure. This is what I feel is dangerous. China should not only cultivate a small number of high-level talents but should improve the knowledge of the general public. I deeply hope that after the general public receives considerable education, they can all implement autonomy and self-defense so that they can stabilize the country internally and resist foreign aggression. Those engaged in education should bear this responsibility. What I have said is not fantasy, nor is it illusion; it is completely based on on-the-spot investigations in China. There are practical experiments in education in Ding County, Shandong, Nanjing, and Wuxi, and that is why I have this idea. It would be best to concentrate the experiences of improving education in various places, add a whole plan, promote it, and transform Chinese society. If we want to achieve the purpose of education reforming society, we must focus on training new education leaders because only with these leaders can we promote new education. This New Education Conference will also discuss how to cultivate new education leaders. I deeply hope that China can have these leaders to engage in the new education of transforming society. We must know that if we want to reform society, there is no way without education. To study the needs of the new society, we must find appropriate education methods and materials. Some schools in China today already have this experiment, which is very admirable. Finally, I hope that China's education will declare independence from Europe and the United States, and the leaders of new education should be cultivated in China based on China's needs. We should not send immature young people to study abroad because foreign educators do not know what China needs. If China needs foreign experts, it can invite them to China to give lectures or establish international higher education institutions. After completing their studies, they can go abroad for further research, which is not impossible. If immature young people go abroad to study, it is actually not very effective. This is what I hope the gentlemen in charge of China's education circle will pay attention to." His words were earnest and sincere, and they are enough to be the medicine for Chinese education. Then Mr. Li Shizeng gave a speech, briefly saying, "Mr. Roger's visit to Shanghai is very short, but today he gave us a very valuable speech, for which we are very grateful. At the same time, we are also very grateful to Mr. Zhu Maocheng for translating it. Now, please, the Datong Music Society will play ancient music, which is also a symbol of the convergence of Eastern and Western cultures." Then the entire Datong Music Society played ancient music, and the meeting did not end until about 1:00 PM.

Establishment of the Municipal Government Security Team 176

Two Regiments with a Total of 3,000 People

Under the Direct Command of the Mayor

Due to the receipt of the war zone, the Shanghai Municipal Government found that the original police force was insufficient for distribution. It had previously submitted a request to the Central Government to transfer 2,000 security team members from Beiping, Nanjing, and Jiangsu to Shanghai to strengthen its force. Now that the takeover matters have been largely completed, the transferred security teams, except for the 1,000 members from Beiping who remain in Shanghai, have all been transferred back to their original defenses. However, the area of this city is vast, and at this time of post-war revitalization, there is inevitably a risk of weak security. Mayor Wu, in view of this, personally went to Beijing to discuss with the Central Government the special circumstances of Shanghai and proposed to follow the example of the provincial governments to establish two municipal security team regiments with a total of 3,000 people to supplement the lack of power of the Public Security Bureau. Each regiment is divided into three battalions, each battalion is divided into three companies, and is equipped with machine gun companies, mounted patrols, automobile teams, armored vehicle teams, and communication teams. This was approved. It is currently being compiled and trained. It is heard that its duties are to assist the Public Security Bureau in maintaining local security. For the suppression of bandits, the arrest of thieves, and the suppression of organized unruly actions, it is responsible without infringing on the powers of the police. In order to avoid regional boundaries and facilitate the agility of mobilization, it is under the direct command of the mayor.

Li Dingrong Appointed Deputy Director by the Two-Road Bureau

The Two-Road Police Department, which was established by the Railway Department's Railway Police Administration Bureau, is officially established today. The director is Ma Shaoping, and the deputy director is also appointed by the Two-Road Bureau as Li Dingrong. The details are as follows:

Received Yesterday Before the establishment of the Police Department, all administrative matters of the Two-Road Police were handled by the staff of the Police Affairs Section of the Road Bureau under the orders of the Police Affairs Section. The establishment of the Two-Road Police Department this time is based on the reorganization of the Police Affairs Section. Yesterday, Fan Shaolian, director of the Police Affairs Section, did not go to the bureau to work. In the morning, Ma Shaoping, the newly appointed director of the Two-Road Police Department, went to the Police Affairs Section to take over and met with Chen Xinghan, director of the Two-Road Bureau, to discuss the organization of the Police Department and all matters related to the exercise of powers in the future.

Established Today After visiting Director Chen, Ma also met with Rong Yi and others, the directors of the police stations of the Two-Roads, to discuss the police affairs of the entire line. The department is scheduled to be established this morning. Ma did not hold an inauguration ceremony when he took office. The Two-Roads Bureau sent Li Dingrong, a former staff member of the Police Affairs Section, to serve as deputy director to assist in all matters. As for the internal staff, most of them are old people from the Police Affairs Section.

Internal Organization Although the department is subordinate to the Ministry of Railways and is directly commanded by the Railway Police Administration Bureau, it must also be directly commanded by the Two-Roads Bureau. However, nominally, it is an independent agency outside the Two-Roads Bureau. Internally, it is divided into four sections: judicial, administrative, general affairs, and police affairs. However, the police affairs section is combined with the police affairs section to facilitate handling affairs.

Minister Gu's Telegram Recently, due to the establishment of railway police stations by the Ministry of Railways on various roads, there have been rumors that the police must be reorganized separately. Yesterday, the staff of the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway Bureaus said that the establishment of the police station was only a reorganization of the original police affairs of the various railway administrations. Therefore, a special telegram was sent to the directors and deputy directors of the police departments of various roads. The telegram is recorded as follows: To the Directors of the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway Bureaus: It is found that the police affairs of various roads have always been under the jurisdiction of the General Affairs Office. Recently, the police affairs along the lines of various roads have been extremely heavy, and the General Affairs Office is the central organization for the collection of documents of the entire bureau. Fearing that it may not be able to take care of everything, the original police affairs department has been reorganized and a police station has been established so that it can take special responsibility and assist in rectification. All police affairs sections and road protection teams of various roads will continue to handle matters as before and have not been reorganized. However, according to recent reports, various rumors have spread outside regarding the reorganization of police affairs on various roads, such as the abolition of the general police section or the reorganization of the road protection team, causing the service personnel to be afraid, etc. It is found that the reported sections not only affect the progress of road affairs but also have a great impact on the security along the lines. They should be strictly prohibited in order to prevent the spread of rumors. In addition to sending separate telegrams, you should also follow the instructions of the director and instruct the police sections and teams under your jurisdiction to be informed and to perform their duties with peace of mind, without believing in rumors or playing with their duties, so as to avoid inconvenience. Local News Two

The Case of Tenants Suing for Rent Exemption in Tongchunfang 179

Reopened Debate Yesterday Morning

Sentenced on the 5th of This Month

The Tongchunfang houses on Beihai Road are the property of the Huamao Company and are rented by the British-owned Aierde Foreign Firm. Currently, the tenants are requesting the landlord to waive the rent for February and March due to the impact of the Sino-Japanese War. However, Aierde believes that Tongchunfang is far away from the war zone at that time, so it is unwilling to accommodate the tenants' request and immediately filed a lawsuit for rent arrears. The case has been tried by the First Special District Local Court, but after waiting for the sentence, it was decided to reopen the debate because there were still investigations that were not completed. Yesterday morning, Li Hu, a judge, opened the court session again. First, the plaintiff's lawyer, Chen Zhongyin, presented a map to the court, proving the location of Tongchunfang. Then, he claimed that the area was a safe zone and was not affected by the war. The defendant should provide reasons for requesting rent reduction or exemption. Then, Le Junying, a lawyer representing eleven tenant households, argued that all rent for February and March should be exempted in fact. At that time, the Japanese army was invading the country, and planes and artillery were bombing day and night. In the Hongkou area, there were incidents of the Japanese army indiscriminately arresting citizens. The entire city was in a state of extreme unease. The City Chamber of Commerce issued a notice to suspend the market uniformly and jointly resist. At this time, the houses had reached a situation of "not holding it for one's own sake," and it was true that a part or all of it could not be used. Most of the defendants are stores, and since they cannot operate, they can request rent reduction or exemption according to the law. Moreover, the rent reduction committee in this city also has a resolution to reduce or exempt rent in order to regulate the financial recovery of the city after the war. Regarding this issue, the municipal government is still discussing it with landlords and tenants, which shows that it is not just the opinion of a few of the defendants. As for the rent after April claimed, it is found that the plaintiff has a kind of contract with the tenants, and lawsuits cannot be filed unless the rent is in arrears for three months, so it has not yet reached the time for repayment. The plaintiff's lawyer then continued to reply, saying that the market strike did not transfer the tenants, and the houses were still being held and used continuously. Moreover, not only was there use but also business income. According to the law, unless there is a fire, water, or other disaster, rent exemption cannot be requested. The measures for exempting house donations due to this incident stipulated by the Municipal Council do not reduce or exempt rent in the central and western districts, and the matter is the same, which can be used as a reference. The rent exemption committee is not a statutory agency, and the resolution is naturally invalid. The discussion of the municipal government is also a mediation nature and cannot forcibly exempt rent. All the owners in the central district are very concerned about this case and regard the judgment of this case as a touchstone. The defendant's lawyer also claimed that although the owners paid much attention to it, the tenants in this city paid more attention to the outcome of this case. After the debate between the two parties was over, Judge Li then scheduled the sentence to be pronounced at 8:00 AM on July 5.

Detective Mistakenly Touches the Trigger and Kills Suspect 180

Why Must the Thief Catcher Carry a Gun to Intimidate?

Yang Weiqi Died a Miserable Death

Yang Weiqi, a native of Chongming, 21 years old, lived at 64 Nanyang Lane, Seymour Road. He sold foreign vegetables in the Seymour Road vegetable market, and his life was quite comfortable. Yesterday afternoon, he went to Yudeci Bathhouse behind the Xian Shi Company with several friends to bathe. After a while, Liu Zhaonian, detective No. 73 of the Yangshupu Police Station, came with an informer and pointed out Yang Weiqi as a suspect in a theft case. Because Liu and others had many people, it was not easy to arrest them. He took out his pistol, aimed at his chest to intimidate him, but mistakenly touched the firing pin. With a bang, the bullet flew out and hit his big belly, cutting off a foot or so of his large intestine. Blood gushed out like a spring, and he was unconscious. The detective car sent him to Tongren Hospital for treatment. It is said that the injury was serious and his life was difficult to save. Because Yang was suspected of a theft case, the police station ordered detectives to take turns guarding him in the hospital. After the incident, according to the reporter's investigation, it turned out that the neighbor Lu Amao's house at 62 Nanyang Lane, Seymour Road, Yang's neighbor, was robbed last month, and silver ornaments and clothes estimated at several hundred yuan were snatched away. The case has not yet been solved. Later, it was discovered that Yang had a major suspicion in this case. Yesterday, he went with Detective Liu to his home to arrest him but failed to do so. He then found out that he was taking a bath in Yudeci, so he followed him to arrest him. According to Yang's friends, Lu Amao also worked in the vegetable business. Because of the jealousy of the same industry, he had always been at odds with Yang Weiqi. The robbery case this time was an outstanding slander, which was wronged and wrong. But in the long run, there will be a day when the truth comes out.

A Woman Was Stabbed to Death in West Shanghai 181

Her Paramour Committed the Murder in the Middle of the Night

A murder case occurred at No. 13 Gaojia Lane, Jiesifeier Road, West Shanghai, at about 5:00 AM yesterday. The deceased was a woman named Tang He, who was stabbed in the neck and abdomen with a sharp knife by her paramour, Shen Qishan, and died. The murderer is 39 years old, a native of Hebei, and served as a soldier in the army. After retiring from the army, he made a living by setting up a meat stall. Last year, he became acquainted with the widow Tang He and lived together at 18 Hele Lane, Changan Road, Zhabei. He had a son named Shengde, who was 22 years old this year, and lived together. After the Sino-Japanese War broke out this spring, he moved to 13 Gaojia Lane, Jiesifeier Road with his son and went to work in a yarn factory to make a living. Shen still stayed in Zhabei until the day before yesterday, when Shen found the address of Tang He's residence and went to look for her again to renew their old relationship. Unexpectedly, the night passed easily, and a murder occurred in the room yesterday morning. It is heard that the two sides had an argument at that time, and Shen immediately stabbed He's neck and abdomen with a sharp knife. He shouted in extreme pain, waking his son Shengde from his sleep. At the same time, Shen Qishan also stabbed his abdomen twice. But one said that Shen's injuries were created by Shengde. Afterwards, the Kangjiaqiao Police Station of the Sixth District Public Security Bureau reported to the headquarters and sent the injured person to the Red Cross for treatment by car. The deceased Tang He, 49 years old this year, had his throat cut off and also had a serious injury to his waist. After the Public Security Bureau reported to the court, the court appointed Prosecutor Wu to inspect the scene and found that the deceased was indeed stabbed to death with a knife before his death.

警備部嚴禁冒充傷兵騷擾 187

Strict Prohibition by the Garrison Headquarters Against Impersonating Wounded Soldiers for Harassment.

Forbidden: Thugs and Ruffians Disturbing the Peace.

Protecting the Iron Will in Exchange for Reputation.

The Songhu Garrison Headquarters issued a public notice yesterday, stating, "Regarding the wounded soldiers who have recovered and are staying in Shanghai, the headquarters and various military units have repeatedly sent personnel to escort them back to their units and have issued notices that they are not allowed to remain in Shanghai. Upon investigation, the wounded soldiers in this anti-Japanese war are all loyal and courageous comrades, and the people of all walks of life admire them. They should strictly abide by discipline to maintain the reputation of the military. However, recent reports indicate that some ruffians and thugs often impersonate wounded soldiers to harass various places, even gathering crowds to extort and destroy public property. We believe that our wounded soldiers have been in the military for many years and have undergone extensive training and would never do such things. We fear that there are one or two unscrupulous individuals, or ruffians and thugs, who are causing trouble under false pretenses, thereby ruining the reputation that the majority have earned with their iron will, which is extremely hateful. Therefore, we hereby issue a strict prohibition and severely prevent this from happening. If such incidents occur in the future, regardless of whether they are wounded soldiers or not, the headquarters will, for the sake of maintaining public order, severely punish them according to the law and will not tolerate them. In addition to dispatching patrols to investigate and apprehend them at any time, the Public Security Bureau is ordered to strictly crack down on them. This notice is hereby issued for public knowledge."

朱慶瀾救濟水災報告（續） 189

Zhu Qinglan's Report on Flood Relief (Continued)

A) Urgent Relief: Urgent relief offices were established, initially headed by myself, and later by Mr. Zha Junliang. Branch offices were established in each disaster area, with special relief commissioners. Relief bureaus were established in each disaster county, with relief directors and staff, to handle urgent relief matters. The meaning of urgent relief is to save lives in times of immediate danger. However, the implementation of this relief effort faced two major difficulties: (1) Relief from floods is not as easy to undertake as relief from droughts or other disasters. In the case of other disasters, except for those who have fled, the fields and lands still exist, and the land can be relied upon. Relief workers can push carts of food and distribute it along the way. However, after a flood, the land is a vast expanse of water. The disaster victims either flee to the hills and wilderness, or cling to the remaining broken sections of the dykes, or crouch on the roofs of collapsed houses, or climb to the tops of tall trees. The suffering of the disaster victims is extreme, and the difficulties faced by the relief workers are also extreme. Usually, the terrain of each area is unknown, and the landmarks have changed. Boats are sent out in all directions, but it is a vast expanse of water. It is easy to get lost. Sailing boats cannot move against the wind, and small boats often run aground. This is why the implementation of urgent relief is difficult, and it is deeply felt by the personnel involved. They are easily blamed by society for not being able to provide widespread relief. (2) The distribution of official relief is not comparable to charity, where philanthropists use their own money and save those in need. Charity trusts the distributors and pays little attention to complicated procedures, while official relief must go through appropriate procedures to ensure verification and demonstrate credibility. In the past, when there were occasional disasters, the government allocated funds for relief, which were mostly handled by the county magistrates through the director, often leading to many abuses. The military did not reach the people. This time, we wanted to correct this malpractice and ensure that all funds and goods were directly verified and distributed by relief personnel. Special regulations were established for verification and distribution, and they were required to follow them. Therefore, the process of creating registers, verifying households, and distributing relief could not be done in a hurry, nor could the procedures be confused and the distribution made vaguely. This is why the handling takes time, and it is easy to be blamed by society for the slow pace of relief. There are the above two major difficulties. If we only consider the government's single-handed relief efforts, only one in ten disaster victims would benefit. Fortunately, at the beginning of the major disaster, the local governments and charitable organizations all provided relief in different ways. More personnel meant wider benefits, and divided responsibilities meant more specialized handling. Thus, the first stage of difficulty was overcome. When the temporary work of all parties was completed, the long-term work of this group began. Then, the relief funds and goods were verified and distributed according to regulations for nine months, and the end has not yet been completely reached. Now, the main points of the method are listed as follows: (To be continued)

Resolved to Join the League for the Abolition of Civil War.

Oppose the Special Business Tax in Jiangsu.

Since the establishment of its meeting place at 15 Xinping Lane, Longmen Road, the Joint Federation of Shanghai Native Place Associations has been actively carrying out its affairs. Yesterday afternoon, the second joint meeting of executive and supervisory committees was held, chaired by Zheng Zhengqiu and recorded by Jiang Changjie. The following resolutions were passed: (1) To join the League for the Abolition of Civil War; (2) To oppose the Jiangsu Provincial Government's imposition of the special business tax. In addition to telegraphing the Executive Yuan to strictly prohibit it, a telegram will also be sent to the Jiangsu Provincial Government to withdraw its order; (3) Regarding the issue of rent reduction in this city, to submit a request to the municipal government to promptly announce the handling measures; (4) To publish a monthly journal; (5) To hold a temporary meeting of the executive committee every half month; (6) To establish the position of executive director in the general affairs department.

甬同鄉會聯席會議紀 192

Minutes of the Joint Meeting of the Ningbo Native Place Association

Solicitation to start August 1st

Resolved to Assist the Northeast Volunteer Army.

Yesterday, the Ningbo Native Place Association in Shanghai convened a joint meeting of the Shanghai Siming Guildhall for the purpose of concluding the Hankou disaster relief efforts. Committee members Yuan Ludeng and Fang Jiaobo were present. Fang Jiaobo chaired the meeting. The chairman first reported on the severe Hankou flood last year, with many natives of Ning and Shao residing in Hankou. Therefore, the Ningbo Native Place Association in Shanghai and the Shanghai Siming Guildhall, along with the Shaoxing Seven Counties Native Place Association in Shanghai, formed a three-group body to organize the Hankou Disaster Relief Society to engage in relief work. Now that the work has been completed, it should be concluded. It was then resolved to donate the remaining funds to the Tanggong project. The association also convened its seventh executive committee meeting at 4:00 PM on the same afternoon. (A) Matters for discussion: 1) The Shaoxing Seven Counties Native Place Association in Shanghai requested a joint claim for the Zhejiang Provincial Construction Two-Five Rent Reduction Method, with modifications. It was resolved to endorse the association's proposal and unanimously advocate for it. 2) Regarding the proposal to establish a permanent memorial for Director Chen Rongguan, it was resolved to join the Shi Gong Meiqing Memorial Association to make it permanent. The name of the memorial association will be reconsidered. 3) Report on the economic situation of this association (summary of income and expenditure report). It was resolved to hold a solicitation to make up for the deficit, scheduled to open on August 1st, and publicly invited Mr. Jin Tingsun to serve as the general captain, and Le Zhenjian, Xu Shengchan, Liu Hongsheng, and Zhang Jiguang to serve as the general staff. (B) Ad Hoc Motions: 1) Regarding the proposal for the Public Works Department to send personnel to solicit opinions from this association regarding the reconstruction of Hengde Lane, adjacent to this association, into a theater, it was resolved that the reconstruction of the theater at that location would cause heavy traffic, which would hinder transportation. In addition to publicly appointing Committee Member Le to inquire about the Public Works Department's letter of opinion, a written statement will also be made. It was also heard that the association's standing committee resolved to allocate 2,000 yuan to assist the Northeast Volunteer Army, to be submitted for retroactive recognition when the special committee meets in the future.

提倡國貨會兩要函 193

Two Important Letters from the Association for the Promotion of National Products.

The Shanghai Citizens' Association for the Promotion of National Products stated that the products of its members were mistakenly identified as enemy goods by the former Anti-Japanese Association, and a considerable number were detained. Chairman Chen Yiting, standing committee members Chen Binghui, Shen Shuyu, Xu Jianruo, Fang Jiange, and others repeatedly provided legal proof to rescue and return the goods. Later, the association was suspended for several months, and the mistakenly detained goods of various factories suffered irreparable damage. Now, it is learned that the Investigation Committee for Detained Goods of the former Anti-Japanese Association has been established and is starting the investigation. In order to protect the interests of members and rescue factories after the war, a special request was submitted to the municipal government yesterday to expedite the return of the goods, and all factories were notified to register within the deadline. The drafts are as follows: (1) A petition to the municipal government stated: "A petition regarding the products of national goods factories and raw materials for manufacturing national goods that were mistakenly detained by the former Anti-Japanese Association, requesting the protection of national goods, understanding of the difficulties of merchants, and a quick instruction to the Investigation Committee to expedite the return of the goods in order to facilitate sales and expand manufacturing. The factories that are members have successively sent letters stating that the products of members and raw materials for manufacturing national goods were mistakenly identified as enemy goods by the former Anti-Japanese Association and have been detained for several months without any definite news of return. Now, it is learned that the Investigation Committee has been established and is starting the investigation. Please take measures to rescue them to avoid damage and maintain national goods, etc. Upon investigation, the former Anti-Japanese Association mistakenly detained a considerable number of products of national goods factories. The delay of several months has caused irreparable losses. At this time of serious national crisis, it is a good opportunity to promote national goods. Moreover, national goods factories have suffered damage from the war and have been greatly weakened, which cannot be restored in a short period of time. The timely establishment of the Investigation Committee deeply admires your understanding of the difficulties of merchants and your intention to protect national goods. This association's responsibility is to promote national goods and protect its members, and it cannot remain silent. It is appropriate to submit a petition requesting that you quickly instruct the Investigation Committee to expedite the return of all mistakenly detained products of national goods factories in order to alleviate commercial difficulties and maintain national goods. The national salvation movement is deeply reliant on this." (2) A notice to all factories stated: "Regarding an important notice: Upon investigation, the former Anti-Japanese Association often mistakenly identified the products of national goods factories as enemy goods and detained them, resulting in great losses and unresolvable grievances. Now, it is learned that the Investigation Committee for Detained Goods of the former Anti-Japanese Association has been declared established and is starting registration. We urge all factories to quickly register the detained goods at 38 Fenglinqiao Road from July 1st to 10th. In order to protect the interests of members and reduce their suffering, in addition to submitting a petition to the municipal government instructing the committee to expedite the return of the mistakenly detained goods of the factories that are members of this association, based on the principle of rescuing post-war losses and assisting the economy of factories, we also plan to collect the detained goods of all members and request them together in order to facilitate their return in the shortest possible time and maintain the interests of members. Therefore, we specifically notify all factories that, when registering, they should send a copy of the detained goods to the association within one week for verification. This matter is important, please do not delay or harm your own rights."

上江航輪失事續訊 194

Further News on the Shangjiang Shipping Accident.

Further news on the Shangjiang merchant ship accident, obtained yesterday, is recorded separately below:

Yongfeng Ship Escapes Danger. The Yongfeng, owned by Shanghai Yitai Foreign Firm, flying the Italian flag, was sailing upstream on the Yangtze River, traveling between Shanghai and Chongqing, carrying passengers and goods. This time, the ship ran aground between Wushan and Chongqing due to bad navigational conditions, causing a large hole in the bow of the ship. The bow cabin was damaged and all the goods were flooded. Later, the shipowner grounded the ship in a shallow area, repaired the hole with cement, and then floated the ship again and towed it to Shanghai. It is now reported that the ship has escaped danger.

Further News on the Wanliu Ship. The Taikoo Company's Shangjiang ship Wanliu ran aground and sank at Huangjiapo on the first of last month. The crew and passengers were rescued by two rice-carrying civilian boats and sent to Yichang. The crew was rescued by the company's Jieding ship. The ship was also carrying 150,000 yuan in silver in Chongqing, which was also dispatched by the company to Huangjiapo and transferred to Hankou. Now, the ship has sunk in the river, leaving only the smokestack and mast visible on the surface.

商圑華隊招募預備員 195

The Chinese Team of the Volunteer Corps Recruits Reservists.

The Chinese team of the International Volunteer Corps recruits reservists every year in accordance with regulations to train and replenish its ranks. It is reported that last year's reservists have completed their training, so it is scheduled to start recruiting this year's reservists from July 1st. The registration office is located at the team's headquarters on the third floor of 11 Hankou Road. The origin of the team is recorded as follows: In 1905, the leaders of Chinese merchants in Shanghai initiated the Shanghai Northern Gymnastics Association, one to protect the security of residents and the other to promote the martial spirit of the people. In 1906, it joined the International Volunteer Corps and became the Chinese team. It has been twenty-eight years since then. Its efforts in defense and its progress in drill and shooting have always been praised by Chinese and Western newspapers and by people of all countries. In recent years, the advanced teams have demonstrated a spirit of catching up, which is evident to everyone. The Volunteer Corps serves the community by maintaining local security. The knowledge of various military skills is knowledge that everyone should have. All healthy people with aspirations should come forward.

The United Association of the Citizens' United Association, the Hongkou District Branches, and the Commercial Associations of Haining Road, North Xizang Road, Aierjin Road, Yangshupu Road, Yinxiang Huade Road, Broadway Road, Hanbile Road, East and West Huade Road, North Jiangxi Road, Baoxing Road, Jiaxing Road, and other areas, totaling more than 20 organizations, has established a joint office. 拐匪猶號哭呼寃 199

Kidnappers Still Crying and Claiming Injustice.

Many Young Children Unclaimed. Shanghai Hongkou Police Station detectives Shi En, Bao Shuji, Bai Mingfu, and others, previously arrested a large number of human traffickers, including the woman Wu Chen and the man Wang Asi, along Zhoujiazui Road and Tangshan Road. Fifteen men and women were arrested, and six boys and girls were rescued. In addition to those claimed by their families, there are eight-year-old girl Lanxiang, eleven-year-old girl Fan Gendi, thirteen-year-old girl Xue Yie, all from north of the Yangtze River, and four-year-old boy Zhihong, from Shaoxing, all of whom remain at the police station. The kidnappers, except for the woman Chen Luo and the man Li Yangxun, five in total, who were found by the police to be unrelated and released, the remaining ten men and women, including Wu Wang, were interrogated by the First Special District Court, and are awaiting sentencing. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen Bingrong came to the First High Court and sentenced the women Wu Chen, Chen Niu, and Zhou Aniang to six two-year sentences for the crime of luring and kidnapping six boys and girls under the age of twenty with the intention of profiting, to be served consecutively for six years. The women Chen Zhu, the men Wang Asi, and Zhang Wenqing were each sentenced to three two-year sentences for the crime of luring and kidnapping three boys and girls under the age of twenty with the intention of profiting, to be served consecutively for four years. Fei Yonggui was sentenced to two two-year sentences for the crime of luring and kidnapping two boys and girls under the age of twenty with the intention of profiting, to be served consecutively for three years. Zhao Zhu and Chen Zhang were each sentenced to one year in prison. The number of days of detention before the judgment was finalized will be counted as two days of imprisonment for each day of detention. Liu Chuntai was found not guilty. The four boys and girls, including Lanxiang, were sent by the police to the China General Association for the Rescue of Women and Children for care. The defendants cried and claimed injustice upon hearing the verdict. The court declared that if they did not agree with the verdict, they could appeal.

旅館内匪黨秘密聚議 200

Bandits Secretly Conspire in Hotel.

Detectives Arrest Eight Robbers.

Guns and Bullets Confiscated.

Yin Zhanqing, a Chinese detective at the General Investigation Department of the General Police Department, discovered that bandits were entrenched in room 30 of the Kader Hotel on Kader Road, secretly conspiring and plotting wrongdoing. Therefore, the previous afternoon, he reported to the Chinese Chief Detective Lu Liankui, who personally supervised detectives Liu Shaokui, Bao Liansheng, Wang Chengying, and western detective Yaman to secretly go and arrest the bandits Zhu Yuwen and Ren Agen. A pistol and seven bullets were confiscated from Zhu. Not long after, six more bandits, Qu Hongsheng, Chen Jinmao, Huang Wu, Ding Zhaoqian, Wang Jinfang, and Wang Haihai, walked into the room. Upon seeing the detectives, Chen immediately threw a pistol with nine bullets inside onto the bed, which was confiscated. Chen and others were arrested, and two more bullets were confiscated. In total, eight bandits were arrested, and two pistols and eighteen bullets were confiscated. They were all taken to the Jing'an Temple Police Station and sent to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District Court yesterday morning. The police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated the above situation, saying that the police had not yet clarified the case, so they had not filed a lawsuit, and requested permission to detain them. Judge Wu Tingqi reviewed the case, questioned the defendants, and ordered that they be detained.

浦灘挖泥挖出草包中骷髏 201

Skeleton Found in Grass Bag Dredged from Pujiang.

Impossible to Distinguish Gender.

Presumably Killed by Japanese Soldiers.

The Hai Xie dredging barge of the Dredging Bureau was dredging mud on the Pujiang River at the Huangpu Wharf in East Shanghai. In the evening, the mud was transported back to the Suzhou River estuary to dump the mud and repair the dam. Suddenly, the mud boat foreman Gao Guifa discovered a grass bag in the mud. Upon opening it, in addition to many bricks and stones, there was also a skeleton. It was impossible to identify the gender. It was then discovered that the grass bag seemed to be a Japanese salted fish bag, but it had turned black. It had probably been submerged at the bottom of the river for several months. The incident was reported to the Customs Water Police Station, which ordered detective Deng Jiagen to investigate. Seeing that the skeleton had no flesh and skin, it was difficult to identify the person. It was taken up, but no one claimed it. Therefore, he ordered the workers to fill it back into the mud dam. It is speculated that it was the body of a Chinese person killed by Japanese soldiers during the Shanghai war and was sunk in the river to destroy the traces.

陳龍盛殺人案 202

Chen Longsheng Murder Case.

Debate Concluded, Awaiting Verdict.

The Yong woman Qi Wu, 42 years old, residing at 88 Xin Kang Li, Tao Wei Road, asked her lodger Chen Longsheng, a Nanking native, for a debt of thirty-nine yuan around 8 p.m. on the 19th of this month. Chen only paid back two yuan, which caused an argument. Chen flew into a rage and took out a small knife from his sleeve, stabbing Wu in the neck nine times, and also stabbing her husband Qi Daxing in the neck. Chen, seeing the great disaster he had caused, fled out the door. Wu was sent to Tongren Hospital, where she died from her injuries. The Yulin Road police, led by detective Gui Shou, arrested Chen at the Xiaoshijie Amusement Park in the city. It was learned that the murder weapon was hidden under the incense burner inside the house at 333 Wuzhou Road, so a secret search was conducted but nothing was found. Later, Chen was captured in the drainage ditch of the patio and brought to the First Special Court. Chen confessed that he had been having an affair with Wu for many years, but because she had started a relationship with someone else, he acted out of anger, etc. Yesterday morning, the hearing continued. The police lawyer Zhang Tianyin said that it was confirmed during the adjournment that the murder weapon belonged to the defendant and that it was intentional homicide, requesting severe punishment. When questioned, the defendant's statement was evasive. Judge Qiao Wanxuan reviewed the confession and ordered that he remain in custody pending sentencing.

嚇詐不理盗竟登門刦掠 203

Ignoring Extortion Leads to Robbery.

Victim Catches One Thief.

Li Dingyi, a resident of 155 Gaochang Temple, Nanshi, has been receiving extortion letters for the past few days, which Li ignored. However, at 10:30 p.m. last night, seven robbers wearing blue cloth shirts and pants, speaking with a Jiangbei accent, suddenly arrived, brandishing pistols, and prohibiting any outcry. They searched and robbed for about half an hour before fleeing with their loot. The tenant Xie Xin lost 18 yuan in cash and a pair of gold earrings. Li lost more than 50 yuan in cash and more than 300 jiao in small change, along with clothing and other items, totaling about 400 yuan. The robbers fled in different directions upon leaving the house. Li secretly followed in close pursuit and caught one thief after chasing him to Paotai Road, Zhouzhao Road. The sentry post there brought the thief and the victim to the Second District Headquarters, awaiting transfer to the Judicial Section for interrogation.

Cai-made Anti-Smoking Solution Is Not an Opium Substitute 204

Cui Daosheng Acquitted

Zheng Ziqian Fined 300 Yuan

On May 13th, Song Bing, Zhang Shaoqing, Ding Zhigao, and other Chinese detectives from the Narcotics Division of the General Inspectorate, having learned that the "Flying Thunder Gaoliang Cai Freedom Anti-Smoking Peace Solution" sold by the Lei Yu Pharmaceutical Company at No. 22 Sanhe Lane, Jiangxi Road, contained toxic substances, went to arrest Cantonese natives Cui Daosheng and Zheng Ziqian. A considerable amount of the solution was seized. The next morning, they were escorted to the First Special District Court. The two defendants were ordered to post bail of 1,500 yuan each, pending a new assessment by the court's forensic doctor. This matter was previously reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Fu Lin continued the hearing in the First Criminal Division. The defendants were represented by lawyer E Sen. The police lawyer, Ru Bao, stated that the police were prosecuting the case under Article 6 of the Anti-Smoking Law, for selling opium substitutes and privately possessing smoking paraphernalia. However, the case seemed to be a scientific issue, dependent entirely on the result of the assessment. If the assessment showed that the solution did not exceed the fixed composition, then it would naturally not be an opium substitute. He inquired whether the court had received the assessment report. Judge Fu then released the forensic doctor's assessment report to both lawyers for review and declared that according to the court's forensic report, the assessment of the solution indicated that it was not an opium substitute but rather a type of nicotine solution. He then ordered the commencement of arguments. After arguments between the police lawyer Ru Bao and the defendant's lawyer E Sen, Judge Fu acquitted Cui Daosheng in court. Zheng Ziqian was found not guilty of selling opium substitutes, but guilty of possessing opium smoking paraphernalia for criminal purposes, and was fined 300 yuan. If he failed to pay the fine, he would be imprisoned for one day for every three yuan. One opium pipe and one opium lamp were confiscated. As for the seized anti-smoking solution, it should be returned to the defendant upon application.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the Shandong coastal area will have southwesterly winds and localized drizzling rain. The East China Sea and the Yangtze River basin will have overcast skies, light fog, and easterly winds. The weather between Taiwan and Luzon will be severe, with cyclones, due to a hurricane that has moved to the northeast-east of Northern Luzon, heading west or northwest-west. Its center was within 60 miles of the intersection of 19 degrees north latitude and 127 degrees east longitude at around 6:00 AM this morning. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the temperature in this city was a high of 82.4 and a low of 68.9. On the same day last year, the high was 92.5 and the low was 76.8.

Letters

To the Esteemed Mr. Chairman,

Yesterday, your newspaper's local news column, under the heading "Record of the General Meeting of the Silk Mill Association," stated, "The strike in various silk mills in Hongkou, demanding improved treatment in all departments, is not the true intention of the union and was caused by incitement from third parties. The truth is not only understood by the industry, but also by various party and government agencies and the trade union." This is far from the truth. The strike was actually caused by employers cutting wages and destroying benefits, causing workers to suffer and making them unable to endure it, thus leading to the strike. If the employers had not cut wages and oppressed the workers, how could a third party incite them to any effect? Furthermore, the same item stated, "The workers in various factories have held several meetings and are very surprised that the demands to restore the original treatment are being published in the newspaper in the name of the colleagues. The workers are deeply aware of the employer's difficulties and are now resuming work to maintain the workers' livelihoods. The resumption of work was agreed upon by both labor and management. In this labor dispute, there are obviously others stirring up trouble. The workers have no demands whatsoever and have already appointed representatives Ji Xiangcheng, Shen Shaoqin, etc., who have signed their names and issued a factual statement in the newspaper, resolving that wages cannot be increased any further and maintaining the status quo." This statement is even more difficult to reconcile with the facts. The workers' demand for improved treatment is a universal expectation. Moreover, the silk mill workers are subjected to the oppressive and harsh treatment of employers, and they suffer terribly. How can they not want to improve their situation? The said Mr. Shen and others obviously have ulterior motives and do not represent the true intentions of all the workers. Fearing that this will confuse the public, we are writing to request a correction. Sincerely, the Shanghai Fourth District Silk Reeling Industry Union, June 30th.

To the Esteemed Mr. Editor of Shen Bao,

Having read the report on the Sanmen Bay inspection in your newspaper on June 30th, it lists Yu Lianpin, the director of the Hangzhou Radio Station. I, the undersigned, am employed by the Zhejiang Provincial Broadcasting Station and am not the director of the radio station. I am writing to request a correction. Sincerely, Yu Lianpin, morning of June 30th.

Free Talk

Aphorisms of Ma Xiangbo, the Nonagenarian

Tang Shaochuan Worked as a Customs Clerk 223

—

In 1872, there was a Cantonese Taiping Rebellion veteran named Rong Hong who surprisingly understood English. He took a group of students to study in the United States. This group of thirty students can be considered the first batch of Chinese students to study abroad. After arriving in the United States, Rong Hong married an American woman. This American woman was a second-marriage woman, so she brought her son from her previous marriage, a "stepson." Later, Rong Hong quarreled with the American woman and separated, dying in the United States. Rong Hong had a very good reputation in the United States because he spoke English very beautifully, so Americans even called him an orator.

From Rong Hong, I am reminded of the first batch of students to study abroad, and from the first batch of students to study abroad, I am reminded of Liang Zhengdong and Tang Shaochuan. Tang Shaochuan and Liang Zhengdong were among the thirty students in this first batch of students to study abroad. After Tang and Liang returned, Li Hongzhang ordered them to enter the Naval Academy to study Chinese. The first batch of students to study abroad were all very young. At that time, the purpose of studying abroad was to learn foreign languages, so it was necessary to send young students abroad, so that it would be easier to read foreign books.

After Tang Shaochuan and Liang Zhengdong graduated from the Naval Academy, I went to Korea and brought them with me to work as foreign language clerks in the Korean customs.

Anecdotes of Resistance Against Aggression 224

— Cai Liang

My friend Mr. Tang once followed the local volunteer army to participate in the war for several months. He recently returned from Xidi. He described the details of the Songhu Anti-Japanese War to me in great detail. Because I believed his words were all personal experiences, I supplemented the following records of matters not found in the newspapers. The Songhu War lasted for a little over a month. The Japanese army's commander had already changed four times. Among them, the momentum was strongest when Ueda came to Shanghai. He commanded about 60,000 troops, equipped by both land and sea. All the latest scientific weapons were available. Coupled with the arrogance of the ultimatum, he had the intention of settling the matter in one battle. At that time, our army had few soldiers and inferior weapons, and the defensive line was meandering for more than forty miles. They were attacked from both sides, and it was almost impossible for the entire army to avoid annihilation. I still remember a certain battle at Miaohang. The defenders of our army's position were only about 500 people, while the enemy came with about three times as many troops, taking advantage of the situation to surround them. The situation was precarious. Fortunately, a certain company of soldiers suddenly came up with a brilliant plan and secretly climbed more than ten elm trees not far from the position with machine guns. They waited for the enemy to sweep and fire. The victims were defeated. However, no one understood where the bullets came from. This is very similar to the divine skill of a certain soldier in Zhabei crouching on the roof of a civilian house and shooting down an airplane with a rifle. One day, when the Japanese planes were dropping bombs on the Zhabei position, each bomb weighed about ten pounds and fell like snowflakes. At this time, our soldiers bravely disregarded their safety, raised their heads, and forced to grab the bombs. Although the bombs fortunately did not explode, the enemy planes were afraid of being shot and flew away. Alas. Our army's resistance to the enemy was so brave and heroic, but in the end, they failed to drive the invaders out of the country. Although it can be said to be the will of Heaven, is it not also a matter of human affairs?

The Reason for Wang Xiaolai's Grief 225

— Sun Choucheng

The other day, during the memorial service for the employees of the Beijing-Shanghai, Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration who died in the national crisis, held at the North Railway Station, Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Chairman Wang Xiaolai's speech was short and rushed, containing endless grief. It was different from his behavior at other memorial services. The next day, Choucheng met with him and asked why he was not as grief-stricken when mourning the fallen soldiers. Why did he almost weep yesterday? He said that when he arrived at the meeting, he saw that the railway station building had been almost completely destroyed by the Japanese army's bombing. Rubble was everywhere, and dangerous walls towered high, which had already greatly stimulated him. When Wang Chunbo read the eulogy, imitating the ancient custom of Shaoxing, with rising and falling tones, as if weeping and complaining, it touched his hometown sentiments. When he heard the families of the deceased employees crying loudly, he couldn't help but feel grief coming from within, almost to the point of tears. Then, he saw among the families of the deceased, white-haired old women with hunched figures, young women with sorrowful eyebrows, and innocent young children who did not understand the world, all wearing black gauze on their arms and huddled in a corner. The widowers, widows, orphans, and destitute were all present before his eyes. Who can be without emotion? How could he not be saddened? According to my original intention, I should have given each person a hundred Yuan coins with Yuan Shikai's image to express my heart. Unfortunately, my current economic ability is not as generous as it was in previous years. My heart is willing, but my strength is insufficient. What can I do? The Japanese soldiers are invading our territory. Those who wear the tiger talisman have the responsibility to defend the territory, but they embrace the policy of non-resistance and allow them to drive straight in and lose important places without hearing of any punishment. Those railway employees, who have no responsibility to defend the territory, were able to embrace the determination to die and, under the enemy's dense aircraft bombs, faithfully and diligently maintain transportation and supply the rear military. They did not care if their heads were broken, their arms were broken, their bones were crushed, or their chests were pierced. Their enthusiasm and perseverance are even greater than the brave generals on the front lines. How can we not respect them?

World News in Brief 226

— Haike

The Japanese are obsessed with kissing films. Although the Japanese nationwide is extremely licentious, they pretend to be upright and dignified on the surface. They appear to be a moral nation of more than three generations. Therefore, they also believe that kissing between men and women is extremely immoral. All European and American films that are imported into their country must undergo strict inspection, and all kissing parts must be completely cut off. English writer J. Street's book "Mysterious Japan" once described this matter. It is said that the work of cutting out kissing scenes in films is hosted by an American hired by the Japanese. He felt sorry for all the beautiful scenes of mouth-to-mouth contact being cut off. Therefore, he specially connected countless cut-off kissing fragments to form a large reel of kissing films. One mouth after another, one lip after another, connected in various ways. He sometimes privately screened them at home for his friends to watch. Everyone said it was a grand spectacle.

A Beautiful Tale of Goldfish 227

— Wu Jiren

Returning from the Goldfish Garden in West Shanghai, I brought back many stories and news about goldfish. Having nothing to do, let me talk about these gleanings.

Goldfish from America. Isn't the journey to America very far? It is quite troublesome to bring them back and forth, unless it is by postal ship. But Americans have great faith in Chinese famous fish. The ship's stewards put their minds to bringing them back. Do you know how they bring them? They used large wooden buckets in Tianjin or Shanghai to scoop up the original water from the fish tanks. Then they put all kinds of fish in them. Isn't the weather hot and cold? They are very careful to keep the temperature of the cabin where the fish buckets are placed consistent. They use air conditioning or ice in hot weather and heaters or radiators in cold weather. In short, they have to keep the temperature consistent so that they can safely arrive in San Francisco and New York. What about eating? There are dried water fleas for sale in Tianjin. It is said that they cost 1.6 yuan per pound. So when they are transported to America, the goldfish will still not be thin and starved to death. That kind of fish-carrying business is also a good business for the ship's stewards.

Xu Guoliang's goldfish. That old fisherman used to raise fish for a living in Beiping. He was brought by the late Shanghai Police Commissioner Xu Guoliang. After the old man arrived in Shanghai, he served General Xu with dozens of tanks of fine species. Later, General Xu was killed, and the attendants dispersed. These many fish were bought by the late Mr. Huang Chujiu and placed in the Great World for care. Later, they were gradually sold out. The large batch was bought by Mr. Mu, who was once a Vice Minister. Mr. Mu was still in Shanghai at the time and cherished those fish like treasures. Soon, he was honored with a position of power. He still begrudged the shipping costs and moved the most beloved tanks to the capital. It is said that there are still many in both Beijing and Shanghai. The old fisherman told me endlessly. When I have time, I will write it down again.

Random Notes on the Art World 228

— Xueni

In times of chaos and separation, there are always many extraordinary people. In history, such as during the Han and Wei dynasties, the Song and Yuan dynasties, and the Ming and Qing dynasties, there were many outstanding, upright, and talented people who were known for their art or established for their character. Such as Ji Kang, Ruan Ji, Wei Zheng, Huang Daozhou, Gu Yanwu, Zhu Da and other peers, can be counted. My friend Chen Zixiao, style name Die, is also an extraordinary person of today. Yu Fan wrote books and was praised in his early years. Meng Yuanlong had the ambition of the sea and lakes and looked down upon others. Over the years, he has traveled mountains and rivers, and his nature has been accustomed to apes and cranes. He wields his brush to write forms, transmitting the Jiangling pink version in the style of Wu Daozi. He has fully acquired the spirit of Huang Gongwang's strangeness and the strength of Zhao Mengfu. Therefore, his free spirit is high in the mist, and his handsome feelings are light as the moon. He detaches himself from the rich and noble floating clouds and escapes from the dust of the world. The other day, he returned from Mount Lu and collaborated with Shou Tie on many pages of fan paintings. One of the paintings is Viewing the Waterfall. He titled it: "I returned from Mount Lu after seeing the waterfall. The strange energy in my chest is chaotic. Uncle Cliff sees a foot of paper from me. The light is full before the small room is opened. A clump of old trees is gathered. The old man carries his hands and his eyebrows are short. The soul of Shi Tao, the spirit of Shi Xi, embraces drunkenness, sings wildly, and cannot turn. I will add a picture of Tianchi for you. The stone walls are thousands of feet high, and the spring is hundreds of feet long. When shall I enter the painting with you and sit and lie down all year without returning?" Reading this poem, his ambition can be seen. This is currently on display in the fan painting exhibition of the Art Appreciation Society in Daqing Lane, Nanjing Road. They are a perfect combination, chasing the creation of nature, and are not ordinary works.

The richness of the content and the exquisiteness of the printing make it a rare product in the recent magazine world. The subscription fee is only three yuan. The deadline has been extended to the end of July.

The Origin of the Old Saying, "Amber Picks Up Mustard Seeds" 230

— Li Mi

Old Ma Xiang discussed the original objects. He said that the sayings "amber picks up mustard seeds" and "lodestone attracts needles" were discovered as early as the Han Dynasty. Mr. Cao Zhongyuan, because he extracted from an English book on wireless telegraphy the statement that our country's Guo Pu invented physics and had this theory, sent a letter to Old Ma Xiang, inquiring about its origin. Old Ma Xiang replied that it was seen in Wang Bi's commentary on the Book of Changes. In my humble opinion, the commentary on the Book of Changes quoted by Old Ma Xiang is actually Kong Yingda's "Correct Meaning" from the early Tang Dynasty, mistakenly taken to be Wang Bi's commentary from the Wei Dynasty. Research shows that the sayings "picks up mustard seeds" and "attracts needles" first appeared in Wang Chong's "Lunheng, Chaotic Dragons" chapter. It says, "Dunmu picks up mustard seeds, lodestone attracts needles, all based on truth, not relying on other things." It also recounts Liu Zijun's handling of the earth dragon ceremony. Huan Junshan questioned whether Dunmu and lodestone could truly pick up needles and mustard seeds. Zijun was at a loss to respond. This historical fact shows that these two sayings existed at the end of the Western Han Dynasty. Wang Chong was a disciple of Ban Biao. When Emperor Suzong was in power, he was almost seventy years old. He was senior to Liu and Huan. Old Ma Xiang's statement that it was discovered in the Han Dynasty, although not explicitly stated, is essentially in agreement. However, it doesn't say "amber picks up mustard seeds" but "Dunmu picks up mustard seeds." Dunmu is tortoise shell. Guo Pu's "Mountain and Sea Classic Picture Praise" says, "Amber picks up mustard seeds." One version replaces amber with tortoise shell. However, amber, when rubbed and heated, can pick up mustard seeds, clearly demonstrating experience, which has been passed down to this day. But there has never been any real evidence that tortoise shell can pick up mustard seeds. My humble opinion is that amber is produced in the Western Regions. Ban Gu's "Book of Han" says it comes from Bin Yuquan. Wei's "Short History" says it comes from Da Qin. It is very clear that it is not native to China. In the first year of Emperor Wu of Han's Baoding era, the Western Regions offered rare treasures, including amber swallows, as seen in Wang Jia's "Lost Records." Emperor Xuan had a precious mirror from India, stored in a tiger-amber tube, as seen in Wu Jun's "Miscellaneous Records of the Western Capital." All these things were considered rare and precious. Probably, when Liu and Huan lived, it was not long after the reigns of Emperors Wu and Xuan. The object was not commonly seen, and the name was not fixed. Because amber's luster resembled tortoise shell, it was mistakenly called Dunmu. Tortoise shell does not truly pick up mustard seeds; it is merely another physical discovery. The annotation to Yu Fan's biography in the "Records of the Three Kingdoms" quotes Wei Zhao's "Book of Wu." It says that when Fan was twelve years old, he wrote to someone, "I have heard that amber does not pick up rotten mustard seeds, and lodestone does not accept crooked needles. Is it not fitting to not dwell on past mistakes?" Here, amber is written correctly. At that time, Fan lived at the end of the Eastern Han Dynasty. When Guo Pu of the Jin Dynasty annotated the "Mountain and Sea Classic" and wrote the "Picture Praise," the "North Mountain Classic Picture Praise" says, "Lodestone attracts iron, amber picks up mustard seeds. The qi has a hidden attraction, and the numbers mysteriously coincide. The attraction of objects is beyond expectation." According to Pu's praise, it is actually based on Dong Zhongshu's "Spring and Autumn Dew Collection, Suburban Language" chapter, which says, "Lodestone attracts iron, pure gold attracts fire. It is strange and amazing, not something people expect." As for Pu's two volumes of "Picture Praise," the original version has long been lost. It exists in the Daoist canon, but it is not the original. Zhang Pu of the Ming Dynasty compiled "Guo Hongnong's Collection" based on the canon version, fully recording the praise text. This is exactly the source that Mr. Cao inquired about, but Old Ma Xiang missed mentioning it. However, the English book on electricity considered it to be an original theory of Guo Pu in the fourth century. Little does it know that elegant sayings are passed down with distant origins. Before Guo Pu was Yu Fan, before Fan was Wang Chong, and before Chong were Liu Xin and Huan Tan. Liu and Huan lived during the reigns of Emperors Ai and Ping, which was at the beginning of the Western era. This is something that should be known. Furthermore, amber is not produced in China. Its discovery of picking up mustard seeds should have been during the Western Han Dynasty. As for lodestone, it first appeared in the "Shen Nong's Materia Medica." By the time of the Yellow Emperor's construction of the south-pointing chariot, the principle of attracting iron had already been discovered. However, the Materia Medica claims that lodestone points south, usually deviating towards the Bing position, because Bing represents great fire, and Geng and Xin metals are controlled by it, which is nothing more than speculation. As the "Lüshi Chunqiu, Profound Understanding" chapter says, "Lodestone summons iron, or draws it." Buwei only mentions lodestone and not amber, which can be taken as evidence that there was no amber during the Qin Dynasty. Therefore, the two sayings "picks up mustard seeds" and "attracts needles," though connected, arose at the end of the Western Han Dynasty, but the physical discoveries and the order of the times have their reasons, which should also be known. Living in solitude without anything to do, I have jotted down these random notes to supplement Old Ma Xiang's incompleteness and to resolve Mr. Cao's confusion.

Li Shizhen's "Compendium of Materia Medica" says that the mustard seeds picked up by amber are actually the grasses of the mustard plant. Lei says that it is a mistake to say "mustard seeds" based on the English book. The meaning seems to also be mustard seeds. Also, Guo Pu's praise of lodestone, quoted in the "Classified Collection of Literary Works" volume six, is not from "Bai Kong's Six Postings." I am including this to inform Mr. Cao and to provide materials for verification.

A Record of Military Courage and Romantic Attachment (96) 231

— Master of the Seeking Happiness Studio

Chapter Eleven: Peeking at the Military Flags in a Small, Remote Town; Flattering and Following the Servants of an Insignificant Group

At the end of Chapter Ten of this book, An Yutian had just met Ye Zuozhang and roughly settled the matter of pacification. After returning to the hotel, he told Liang Xiaoyun the details. Upon hearing that the official business had been handed over to the Chief of Staff by Ye Zuozhang, Liang Xiaoyun suggested that they should give some face to the Chief of Staff who was handling the matter. She told An Yutian to specifically pay a visit to the Chief of Staff the next day, humbly asking him for guidance and attention in everything, so that the official document could be processed and issued quickly in order to proceed rapidly. The name of this Chief of Staff was Bai Shanxun. Among all the senior military officers under Ye Zuozhang, he was considered the best of the mediocre. He had graduated from a military academy in Japan and was not an ignorant fool. However, since he had attached himself to a warlord as Chief of Staff, he had to comply with the wishes of his supervisor in everything. After seeing An Yutian, he said coldly with a stern face, "I am the most agreeable person. Whatever the Old General asks me to do, I will only comply and not offer any other opinions. Your official document will be processed in half a day and someone will be sent to deliver it to you. As for the rest, we'll talk about it later." After saying this, he returned to his seat by his desk and continued to review documents as usual, ignoring An Yutian. An Yutian did not want to disturb him further and politely took his leave. The Chief of Staff nodded slightly but did not get up to see him off. Fortunately, An Yutian had gained some experience by this time and knew that the reason Chief of Staff Bai was giving him the cold shoulder was not because he was genuinely dissatisfied with him or looked down on him, but because the issue of gifts and personal connections was still at play. After discussing it again with Liang Xiaoyun upon his return, they originally intended to use the same old method of dealing with Section Chief Wan Chengqi and clear this path as well. However, unexpectedly, the official document was delivered the next day. After rewarding the messenger soldier with ten dollars and leaving the official document behind, the hotel's accountant, servants, and chauffeur all received this information. They all came to congratulate them. The couple was so happy that they temporarily put aside the matter of taking care of Chief of Staff Bai. Afterwards, they spent another two days together going to the government office to thank Ye Zuozhang and the Fifth Madam, and visiting guests everywhere, connecting with all the important people in the Governor's office. Only then did they gradually find some leisure.
